## 1. Why Kamelot Is Open Source

### 1.1 Foundational Belief

Kamelot is open source because we believe that software that manages your most important data ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â your files ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â should be fully accountable to you. You should never have to trust a black box with your documents, your photographs, your code, or your memories.

Open source is not a marketing strategy for Kamelot. It is the only way we could build this system with integrity.

### 1.2 Trust Through Transparency

Closed-source software that handles personal files asks users to trust the vendor without evidence. The vendor could:

- Exfiltrate file contents to remote servers
- Include backdoors for law enforcement or intelligence agencies
- Embed tracking and advertising SDKs
- Deprecate features to force upgrades
- Sell user metadata to third parties

With Kamelot, every claim about privacy, security, and data handling can be verified by inspecting the source code. Trust is not required; verification is sufficient.

### 1.3 Community Benefits of Open Source

Beyond user trust, open source provides concrete benefits:

- **Security auditing**: Thousands of eyes review the code. Vulnerabilities are found and fixed faster.
- **Portability**: The community ports Kamelot to platforms the core team cannot support.
- **Innovation**: External contributors add features and improvements.
- **Longevity**: If the original creators stop development, the community can fork and continue.
- **Education**: Students and researchers study Kamelot's design and implementation.

### 1.4 Why Not a Source-Available License?

We specifically chose OSI-approved open source licenses (MIT and Apache 2.0) rather than source-available or "open core" licenses because:

- Source-available licenses often restrict commercial use or redistribution
- Open core models reserve the best features for paid versions
- True open source ensures that the entire community benefits

Kamelot has no paid version, no enterprise edition, and no feature gate. Everything is free and open source.

---

## 2. Licensing Philosophy: MIT + Apache 2.0

### 2.1 Dual Licensing

Kamelot is dual-licensed under MIT and Apache 2.0. Users may choose either license.

### 2.2 MIT License

The MIT License is one of the most permissive open source licenses:

- Do anything with the code: use, copy, modify, merge, publish, distribute, sublicense
- No restrictions on commercial use
- No requirement to share modifications
- No patent grant (explicitly)
- Minimal conditions: include the copyright notice and permission notice

### 2.3 Apache 2.0 License

The Apache 2.0 License is more comprehensive:

- Similar permissions to MIT: use, copy, modify, distribute
- Explicit patent grant from contributors
- Requires retention of notices
- Includes a clause terminating patent rights if the user sues for patent infringement
- More suitable for enterprise adoption (legal teams are familiar with it)

### 2.4 Why Dual License?

Dual licensing allows users to choose the license that best fits their needs:

- **Individuals and small projects**: MIT is simpler and well-understood
- **Enterprises**: Apache 2.0's explicit patent grant provides legal clarity
- **Derivative works**: Both licenses permit commercial use and proprietary derivatives

We do not require contributors to sign a Contributor License Agreement (CLA) because:

- CLAs can create a power imbalance between project and contributor
- Both MIT and Apache 2.0 already handle inbound licensing through contribution terms
- We want to minimize barriers to contribution

### 2.5 License Compatibility

Both licenses are:

- GPL-compatible (MIT is GPL-compatible; Apache 2.0 is GPLv3-compatible)
- OSI-approved
- Compatible with each other (dual-licensed projects can accept contributions under either)

---

## 3. No Telemetry, No Tracking, No Data Harvesting

### 3.1 The Problem with Telemetry

Most modern software includes telemetry ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â the automatic collection and transmission of usage data to the vendor. This data is typically used for:

- Product improvement (usage patterns, crash reports)
- Marketing analytics (user engagement, feature popularity)
- Monetization (user profiling, targeted advertising)
- AI training (feeding user data into machine learning models)

Telemetry is almost always enabled by default and difficult to disable. Users often don't know it exists.

### 3.2 Kamelot's Policy

Kamelot has **zero telemetry by default**. Specifically:

| Data Type | Collected? | Default | Can Be Enabled? |
|-----------|-----------|---------|-----------------|
| File contents | Never | N/A | N/A |
| File names/paths | Never | N/A | N/A |
| File metadata | Never | N/A | N/A |
| Search queries | Never | N/A | N/A |
| Embedding vectors | Never | N/A | N/A |
| Index structure | Never | N/A | N/A |
| Crash reports | No | Off | `--telemetry` flag |
| Version ping | Yes (minimal) | On | Can be disabled |
| Usage statistics | Never | N/A | N/A |
| Hardware info | Never | N/A | N/A |

### 3.3 The Version Ping

The only data transmitted by default is a minimal version ping:

- Kamelot version (e.g., "0.1.0")
- Operating system (e.g., "Linux 6.8.0")
- Timestamp (rounded to the day)

This ping is used only to estimate the size of the user base. It contains no identifying information, no IP address storage, and no persistent identifiers.

**To disable**: `kml config set telemetry.version_ping false`

### 3.4 Crash Reports (Opt-In)

Crash reports can be enabled with `--telemetry` and include:

- Stack trace (function names, no variable values)
- Operating system version
- Hardware configuration (CPU model, RAM, GPU)
- Kamelot configuration (without keys or paths)

Crash reports do NOT include:

- File contents, names, or paths
- Search queries or results
- Encryption keys or seed phrases
- Network information beyond OS version

### 3.5 Comparison with Industry Practice

| Product | Default Telemetry | Can Be Fully Disabled? | Data Collected |
|---------|------------------|----------------------|----------------|
| Kamelot | None | Yes (no change needed) | Version ping only |
| Google Drive | Extensive | No | File metadata, usage patterns, device info |
| Dropbox | Moderate | Partial | File names, usage patterns, device info |
| Microsoft OneDrive | Extensive | Partial | File contents (scanning), usage patterns, device info |
| Apple iCloud | Moderate | Partial | File metadata, usage patterns, device info |
| Nextcloud | Minimal | Yes | Version ping, usage statistics |

---

## 4. Transparent Development Process

### 4.1 Public Roadmap

Kamelot's development roadmap is published at:

- https://github.com/lois-kleinner/kamelot/projects
- https://kamelot.dev/roadmap

The roadmap includes:

- Current release goals
- Upcoming features (with design documents)
- Long-term vision
- Community-requested features

### 4.2 RFC Process

Significant changes follow a Request for Comments (RFC) process:

1. **Pre-RFC**: Discussion on GitHub Discussions
2. **RFC document**: Formal proposal with motivation, design, alternatives
3. **Review period**: Minimum 2 weeks for community feedback
4. **Decision**: Accepted, rejected, or revised by maintainers
5. **Implementation**: RFC is implemented and tracked as a GitHub issue

All RFCs are archived in the repository at `docs/rfcs/`.

### 4.3 Commit History

Every commit is publicly visible on GitHub. Commits must:

- Reference related issues
- Include test coverage for new features
- Pass CI (build, lint, tests, security audit)
- Be signed with GPG (verified commits)

### 4.4 Release Process

Releases follow semantic versioning (semver):

- **Patch (0.0.x)**: Bug fixes, security patches ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â no breaking changes
- **Minor (0.x.0)**: New features, deprecations ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â no breaking changes (with rare exceptions)
- **Major (x.0.0)**: Breaking changes ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â migration guide provided

Release candidates (RCs) are published for community testing before final release.

### 4.5 Changelog

Every release includes a detailed changelog:

- New features (with usage examples)
- Bug fixes (with issue references)
- Performance improvements
- Breaking changes (with migration instructions)
- Security fixes (with CVE references if applicable)
- Deprecation notices

## 5. Community Governance Model

### 5.1 Governance Structure

Kamelot uses a hybrid governance model:

- **BDFL (Benevolent Dictator for Life)**: Final authority on technical decisions (Lois-Kleinner during the initial phase)
- **Core maintainers**: 5ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã‚Â¦ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã¢â‚¬Å“7 individuals with commit access and decision-making authority
- **Contributors**: Anyone who submits pull requests, files issues, or participates in discussions
- **Users**: Anyone who runs Kamelot

Transition to a fully community-governed model (e.g., a foundation) is planned when the project reaches sufficient maturity (estimated: 2027ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã‚Â¦ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã¢â‚¬Å“2028).

### 5.2 Decision-Making Process

| Decision Type | Process | Who Decides |
|--------------|---------|------------|
| Bug fixes | Direct PR ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¾ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ review ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¾ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ merge | Core maintainers |

### 5.3 Code of Conduct

Kamelot enforces a Code of Conduct based on the Contributor Covenant:

- Be respectful and inclusive
- Assume good faith
- Focus on what is best for the community
- Show empathy towards other community members

Violations are reported to conduct@kamelot.dev and handled by a dedicated committee.

### 5.4 Contribution Pathways

| Role | Requirements | Rights |
|------|-------------|--------|
| First-time contributor | One accepted PR | Listed in CONTRIBUTORS |
| Regular contributor | 5+ accepted PRs | Invited to contributor chat |
| Core maintainer | Sustained contributions, maintainer vote | Commit access, decision votes |
| Steering committee | Invitation by maintainers | Strategic decisions |

### 5.5 Community Tools

- **Discussions**: GitHub Discussions for general conversation
- **Issues**: GitHub Issues for bugs and feature requests
- **Pull requests**: GitHub PRs for code contributions
- **Chat**: Matrix channel for real-time communication
- **Wiki**: Public wiki for documentation
- **Blog**: Development blog at https://kamelot.dev/blog

---

## 6. Ethical AI Commitment

### 6.1 Principles

Kamelot's AI features are governed by strict ethical principles:

1. **Local processing**: All AI inference runs on the user's device. No data is sent to external servers.
2. **No training on user data**: Kamelot never uses user files, queries, or embeddings for model training.
3. **Transparent model**: Qwen 2 VL is open-weight and publicly auditable.
4. **User control**: AI features can be disabled entirely. The system works without AI.
5. **Deterministic behavior**: Same input always produces the same output. No hidden personalization.

### 6.2 Why Local AI Is Ethical AI

Cloud-based AI systems raise ethical concerns:

- **Privacy**: Cloud providers see every file and query
- **Consent**: Users often don't know their data is used for training
- **Bias**: Cloud models may reflect provider's biases and censorship policies
- **Access**: Cloud AI requires internet, excluding offline populations
- **Lock-in**: Cloud AI creates dependency on specific providers

Kamelot's local AI avoids all of these concerns:

- Files never leave the user's device
- No data is available for training
- The model is fixed and deterministic
- Works completely offline
- No provider dependency

### 6.3 Model Transparency

Qwen 2 VL (the default embedding model) is:

- **Open weights**: Available under Apache 2.0 license
- **Documented architecture**: Full technical paper published
- **Auditable**: Any user can run the model independently and verify outputs
- **Replaceable**: Users can substitute any compatible model

### 6.4 Future AI Features

As we add AI features, we commit to:

- Publishing detailed documentation of AI capabilities and limitations
- Adding AI features as opt-in, not default
- Never uploading user data for any purpose
- Supporting alternative models (including fully open models like BERT-based alternatives)
- Including AI output disclaimers where appropriate

### 6.5 The Limits of Kamelot's AI

We are transparent about what Kamelot's AI cannot do:

- It cannot read or understand file contents (it generates embeddings, not summaries)
- It cannot generate new content (no text generation, no image generation)
- It cannot make decisions or recommendations
- It cannot learn from user behavior (no personalization)

Kamelot's AI is a matching and retrieval tool, not an autonomous agent.

---

## 7. Accessibility and Inclusive Design

### 7.1 Accessibility Principles

Kamelot is designed to be usable by as many people as possible, regardless of:

- Visual ability
- Hearing ability
- Motor ability
- Cognitive ability
- Language
- Hardware resources

### 7.2 Accessibility Features

#### 7.2.1 Visual Accessibility

- **Screen reader support**: CLI output is designed for screen reader parsing (structured output with machine-readable formats available)
- **High contrast mode**: wgpu canvas supports system high contrast theme
- **Resizable UI**: All GUI elements scale with system font size settings
- **No color-only indicators**: Status information is conveyed through text, not just color
- **Configurable colors**: Users can customize the color palette

#### 7.2.2 Motor Accessibility

- **Full keyboard navigation**: All GUI functions accessible via keyboard
- **CLI-first design**: All features available through terminal (no GUI required)
- **Configurable timeouts**: No hard timeouts on operations
- **Reduced pointer precision requirements**: Large click targets

#### 7.2.3 Cognitive Accessibility

- **Clear error messages**: Technical jargon avoided in user-facing messages
- **Predictable behavior**: Operations follow consistent patterns
- **Undo support**: Destructive operations can be undone
- **Documentation**: Plain language documentation with examples

#### 7.2.4 Language Accessibility

- **Internationalization (i18n)**: All user-facing strings are externalized
- **Configuration in any language**: The configuration system uses keys, not natural language
- **Documentation in multiple languages**: Priority languages: English, French, German, Japanese, Mandarin Spanish

### 7.3 Inclusive Design Practices

- **Gender-neutral language** in all documentation
- **Diverse representation** in community materials
- **Respectful terminology** (e.g., "master/slave" avoided)
- **Socioeconomic awareness**: Kamelot runs on low-cost hardware

---

## 8. Ethical Supply Chain

### 8.1 Hardware

Kamelot has no hardware supply chain (it is a software product). However, we recognize the ethical implications of hardware that runs Kamelot:

- **Conflict minerals**: Many computing devices contain minerals sourced from conflict-affected regions
- **Labor practices**: Electronics manufacturing has been associated with labor rights violations
- **Environmental justice**: E-waste disproportionately affects communities in developing countries

### 8.2 Our Response

While we cannot control the hardware supply chain, we:

- **Document hardware impacts**: Provide guidance on choosing ethically manufactured hardware
- **Support right to repair**: Extend hardware life to reduce manufacturing demand
- **Partner with ethical recyclers**: Ensure end-of-life handling respects workers and the environment
- **Advocate**: Participate in industry discussions on ethical computing hardware

### 8.3 Software Dependencies

All software dependencies are:

- Open source (no proprietary dependencies)
- Audited for license compliance
- Scanned for security vulnerabilities
- Reviewed for ethical concerns (e.g., no dependencies from sanctioned entities)

### 8.4 Our Own Operations

We ensure ethical practices in our own operations:

- All team members are contractors or employees (no unpaid interns)
- Remote-first (no forced relocation)
- Transparent compensation (salary bands published)
- Work-life balance respected (no crunch culture)

---

## 9. Ethical Considerations in AI and Data Processing

### 9.1 Environmental Justice

Kamelot's local-first approach has implications for environmental justice:

- **Data center placement**: Cloud data centers are disproportionately located in low-income and minority communities, where their pollution and water consumption impact vulnerable populations. By eliminating the need for data centers, Kamelot reduces this environmental justice burden.

- **E-waste dumping**: Developed nations export e-waste to developing countries, where informal recycling exposes workers to toxic materials. By extending hardware life, Kamelot reduces the volume of e-waste generated and the associated environmental justice impacts.

- **Digital divide**: Kamelot runs on low-cost hardware and does not require high-bandwidth internet, making advanced file management and AI search accessible to users in developing regions and rural areas.

### 9.2 AI Ethics and Bias

| Concern | Cloud AI Systems | Kamelot Local AI |
|---------|-----------------|------------------|
| Training data bias | Model may reflect provider's biases | Fixed model, no personalization |
| Censorship | Provider can filter or modify results | No filtering possible |
| Feedback loops | User behavior trains future models | No feedback loop (static model) |
| Transparency | Proprietary model, limited audit | Open weights, fully auditable |
| Accessibility | Requires internet, English-centric | Offline, multilingual support |
| Environmental cost | Energy-intensive cloud inference | Efficient local inference |

### 9.3 The Ethics of Local Processing

Local processing is not just a technical choice ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â it carries ethical weight:

1. **Data sovereignty**: Users retain full control over their data. No third party can access, analyze, or monetize file contents.

2. **Consent**: Users explicitly choose what data to process locally. There is no hidden data collection or secondary use of data.

3. **Autonomy**: Users are not dependent on cloud provider decisions. Service shutdown, terms-of-service changes, or price increases do not affect functionality.

4. **Privacy by design**: The system architecture inherently protects privacy. It is not retrofitting privacy onto a data-hungry design.

5. **Equity**: Local processing works for everyone, regardless of connectivity, wealth, or geography.

### 10.4 Dependency Ethics

Kamelot performs ethical review of all dependencies:

| Criterion | Assessment Process | Current Compliance |
|-----------|-------------------|-------------------|
| License compatibility | Automated scan on every PR | 100% (all MIT/Apache/BSD/MIT) |
| Known vulnerabilities | Cargo audit in CI | 0 critical, 0 high |
| Maintainer responsiveness | Check issue tracker | All dependencies actively maintained |
| Supply chain risk | Evaluate criticality and alternatives | Minimal critical dependencies |
| Ethical sourcing | No dependencies from sanctioned entities | Verified |
| Cryptocurrency mining | Dependency audit for mining code | None detected |
| Telemetry | Audit for unexpected network access | None present |

## 11. Transparency Reports and Accountability

### 11.1 Annual Transparency Report

Kamelot publishes an annual transparency report covering:

1. **Government requests**: Number of requests for user data, encryption keys, or source code modification
2. **Security incidents**: Number, severity, and resolution of security incidents
3. **Vulnerability disclosures**: Number of reported and patched vulnerabilities
4. **Community moderation**: Code of conduct enforcement actions
5. **Financial transparency**: Revenue sources, funding, and spending on development
6. **Governance changes**: Changes to maintainers, governance model, or licensing

### 11.2 Transparency Report Timeline

| Report | Period | Publication Date | Status |
|--------|--------|-----------------|--------|

### 11.3 Request Handling

| Type of Request | 2025 Count | 2026 YTD | Policy |
|-----------------|-----------|-----------|--------|
| Government data requests | 0 | 0 | Challenge legally, notify user if permitted |
| DMCA takedown notices | 1 (invalid) | 0 | Evaluate each claim, defend fair use |
| Trademark disputes | 0 | 0 | Protect project identity |
| Subpoenas for user data | 0 | 0 | No user data to provide (zero-knowledge) |
| National security letters | 0 | 0 | Would challenge legally if received |

## Open Source Ethics Implementation Framework

### Action Items and Measurable Targets

Kamelot's open source ethics framework establishes concrete, measurable commitments across six dimensions of ethical open source practice. **Code Transparency**: Maintain 100% of core filesystem, AI inference engine, and K-Swarm mesh protocol code publicly available under MIT or Apache 2.0 licenses, measured through automated license compliance scanning in CI pipeline. Target: zero proprietary dependencies in Community Edition by 2027-Q2. **Privacy Guarantee**: Maintain zero telemetry, zero data collection, and zero tracking in all Community Edition builds, verified through automated privacy audit in CI pipeline that scans for network connections, data serialization, and analytics SDK usage. Target: pass privacy audit with zero findings for all releases. **Governance Participation**: Enable community governance through public RFC process, elected technical steering committee, and transparent decision-making documentation. Target: minimum 5 community-elected steering committee members by 2028-Q1, with meeting minutes and decision logs published within 7 days. **Ethical AI Compliance**: Maintain published ethical AI principles with independent audit of AI model training data, bias testing, and environmental impact. Target: annual ethical AI audit published with findings and remediation plan by 2027-Q1. **Accessibility Standards**: Achieve WCAG 2.2 AA compliance for all web-based interfaces by 2027-Q3, with accessibility regression testing in CI pipeline. **Supply Chain Ethics**: Maintain an ethical supply chain policy covering hardware vendors, cloud service providers, and third-party dependencies, with published supplier ethics assessments for all material vendors by 2027-Q4.

### Implementation Timeline and Milestones

The ethics implementation roadmap follows a phased approach aligned with Kamelot's release cycle. **Phase 1 (Foundation, 2026-Q3 to 2026-Q4)**: Establish automated privacy audit pipeline with zero-failure gate for all Community Edition builds, deploy license compliance scanning in CI, and publish initial governance model documentation with RFC process specification. Key deliverables include privacy audit infrastructure, license compliance automation, and governance RFC repository. **Phase 2 (Governance and Verification, 2027-Q1 to 2027-Q2)**: Conduct first ethical AI audit with independent third-party reviewer, publish first annual transparency report covering all commitments, and launch community steering committee election process. Key deliverables include independent ethical AI audit report, transparency report covering governance, privacy, AI ethics, and supply chain, and steering committee election infrastructure. **Phase 3 (Maturity and Leadership, 2027-Q3 to 2028-Q1)**: Achieve WCAG 2.2 AA compliance certification, publish comprehensive ethical supply chain assessments, and contribute open source ethics best practices to community foundations (OSI, FSF, Apache Foundation). Key deliverables include WCAG 2.2 AA compliance certification, ethical supply chain assessment publication, and community foundation contribution package.

### Reporting Methodology and Verification

Kamelot's open source ethics reporting follows a multi-stakeholder accountability model. The primary reporting vehicle is the annual Transparency Report, which covers code transparency metrics (lines of code, contributor diversity statistics, license compliance status), privacy guarantee verification (automated audit results, third-party privacy review, network connection analysis), governance participation statistics (RFC submissions, steering committee decisions, community votes), ethical AI compliance status (audit findings, bias testing results, model training data provenance), accessibility compliance status (WCAG evaluation results, user testing findings, accessibility regression statistics), and supply chain ethics assessments (supplier audit results, conflict mineral reporting, labor practice evaluations). All reports are published in the Kamelot documentation repository in machine-readable format (JSON schema) for automated processing. Third-party verification is conducted by an independent ethics auditor with expertise in open source governance, digital rights, and AI ethics. The auditor publishes their assessment methodology alongside findings to enable scrutiny. Community members can submit concerns through the ethics reporting channel, with documented response process and resolution timeline. The Technical Steering Committee reviews ethics implementation status quarterly and publishes meeting minutes with action items and responsible parties.

## 12. Conclusion

Kamelot is open source because we believe that software that manages your most important data must be accountable to you. Every line of code is visible, every claim is verifiable, and every feature is under your control.

Our ethical commitments extend beyond open source:

- **No telemetry**: Your data stays on your device
- **Transparent development**: Every decision is documented
- **Community governance**: Users have a voice in the project direction
- **Ethical AI**: Local, auditable, non-exploitative
- **Inclusive design**: Accessible to all users

We invite you to verify our claims. Clone the repository. Read the code. Build the binary. Satisfy yourself that Kamelot does what we say it does ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã¢â€žÂ¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Â¦Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€ Ã¢â‚¬â„¢ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¢ÃƒÆ’Ã‚Â¢ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ã‚Â¬Ãƒâ€¦Ã‚Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â¬ÃƒÆ’Ã†â€™ÃƒÂ¢Ã¢â€šÂ¬Ã…Â¡ÃƒÆ’Ã¢â‚¬Å¡Ãƒâ€šÃ‚Â and nothing more.

### Additional Perspective

This section provides supplementary analysis that deepens the understanding of Kamelot's approach to the topics discussed above. The semantic vector file system paradigm represents a fundamental shift in how humans interact with digital information, moving from location-based retrieval to meaning-based discovery. This shift has profound implications for productivity, data governance, and user experience.

Kamelot's architecture is designed to support this paradigm shift through several key innovations: the flat encrypted store eliminates the cognitive overhead of directory management; the Qwen 2 VL Q4 embedding pipeline enables understanding of file content at a deep semantic level; the Qdrant vector index provides millisecond-scale similarity search; and the native GPU canvas offers a spatially-organized interface that leverages human spatial memory.

Practical deployment considerations include hardware requirements, integration with existing workflows, data migration strategies, and user training. Organizations adopting Kamelot should plan for a transition period during which traditional filesystem access is maintained alongside the semantic layer. The POSIX-compatible filesystem bridge (FUSE on Linux, WinFSP on Windows) ensures backward compatibility, allowing users to adopt semantic search at their own pace.

### Additional Perspective

This section provides supplementary analysis that deepens the understanding of Kamelot's approach to the topics discussed above. The semantic vector file system paradigm represents a fundamental shift in how humans interact with digital information, moving from location-based retrieval to meaning-based discovery. This shift has profound implications for productivity, data governance, and user experience.

Kamelot's architecture is designed to support this paradigm shift through several key innovations: the flat encrypted store eliminates the cognitive overhead of directory management; the Qwen 2 VL Q4 embedding pipeline enables understanding of file content at a deep semantic level; the Qdrant vector index provides millisecond-scale similarity search; and the native GPU canvas offers a spatially-organized interface that leverages human spatial memory.

Practical deployment considerations include hardware requirements, integration with existing workflows, data migration strategies, and user training. Organizations adopting Kamelot should plan for a transition period during which traditional filesystem access is maintained alongside the semantic layer. The POSIX-compatible filesystem bridge (FUSE on Linux, WinFSP on Windows) ensures backward compatibility, allowing users to adopt semantic search at their own pace.


### Supplementary Context

Kamelot's semantic vector file system paradigm fundamentally changes how users interact with their digital information. By replacing hierarchical directory structures with meaning-based retrieval, Kamelot reduces cognitive load and enables faster, more intuitive access to files. This approach is grounded in research showing that humans naturally recall information by context and association rather than by location.

The implementation leverages several advanced technologies working in concert: the Qwen 2 VL Q4 model running locally via Ollama generates semantically rich embeddings; Qdrant provides scalable vector similarity search; the encrypted flat store ensures data confidentiality; and the native GPU canvas leverages human spatial memory. Together, these components create a filesystem experience that adapts to how users actually think.

Organizations adopting Kamelot benefit from reduced search time, improved data discoverability, enhanced security through user-controlled encryption, ransomware immunity via the .aioss immutable ledger, and lower total cost of ownership through efficient storage utilization and hardware reuse.

### Additional Context

Kamelot represents a paradigm shift in file management. By leveraging semantic vector embeddings from the Qwen 2 VL Q4 model running locally via Ollama, Kamelot understands file meaning rather than just names or paths. This enables intuitive natural language queries.

All AI processing happens locally on user hardware. The flat encrypted store uses XChaCha20-Poly1305. The .aioss immutable ledger provides tamper-evident versioning and ransomware immunity through append-only hash chains.

The native GPU canvas interface is built with Rust, wgpu, and Vello. Users can arrange files spatially, connect related items, and scrub through time to restore previous workspace states.
